<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Surgery</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Use of incisive instruments on a person to investigate or treat a medical condition</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the medical specialty. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Surgery_(disambiguation)" title="Surgery (disambiguation)">Surgery (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

.thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Surgeons_at_Work.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="833" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Surgeons_at_Work.jpg/200px-Surgeons_at_Work.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Surgeons_at_Work.jpg/400px-Surgeons_at_Work.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Surgeons conducting operations</div></div></div></div>
<p><b>Surgery</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[a]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Medical_specialty" title="Medical specialty">medical specialty</a> that uses operative manual and instrumental techniques on a person to investigate or treat a pathological condition such as a disease or injury, to help improve bodily function, appearance, or to repair unwanted ruptured areas.
</p><p>The act of performing surgery may be called a <b>surgical procedure</b>, <b>operation</b>, or simply "surgery". In this context, the verb "operate" means to perform surgery. The adjective <b>surgical</b> means pertaining to surgery; e.g. <a href="/wiki/Surgical_instrument" title="Surgical instrument">surgical instruments</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surgical_nurse" title="Surgical nurse">surgical nurse</a>. The person or subject on which the surgery is performed can be a person or an animal. A <a href="/wiki/Surgeon" title="Surgeon">surgeon</a> is a person who practices surgery and a <a href="/wiki/Surgeon%27s_assistant" title="Surgeon's assistant">surgeon's assistant</a> is a person who practices surgical assistance. A surgical team is made up of the surgeon, the <a href="/wiki/Surgeon%27s_assistant" title="Surgeon's assistant">surgeon's assistant</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Anesthesiology" title="Anesthesiology">anaesthetist</a>, a circulating nurse and a <a href="/wiki/Surgical_technologist" title="Surgical technologist">surgical technologist</a>. Surgery usually spans from minutes to hours, but it is typically not an ongoing or periodic type of treatment. The term "surgery" can also refer to the place where surgery is performed, or, in <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>, simply the office of a <a href="/wiki/Doctor%27s_office" title="Doctor's office">physician</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dentist" title="Dentist">dentist</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Veterinarian" title="Veterinarian">veterinarian</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Surgery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leikkaus_Punaisen_ristin_sairaalassa_Tampereella_(26875894332).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2465" data-file-width="3924" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Leikkaus_Punaisen_ristin_sairaalassa_Tampereella_%2826875894332%29.jpg/220px-Leikkaus_Punaisen_ristin_sairaalassa_Tampereella_%2826875894332%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Leikkaus_Punaisen_ristin_sairaalassa_Tampereella_%2826875894332%29.jpg/330px-Leikkaus_Punaisen_ristin_sairaalassa_Tampereella_%2826875894332%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Leikkaus_Punaisen_ristin_sairaalassa_Tampereella_%2826875894332%29.jpg/440px-Leikkaus_Punaisen_ristin_sairaalassa_Tampereella_%2826875894332%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leikkaus_Punaisen_ristin_sairaalassa_Tampereella_(26875894332).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Surgery underway at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Cross" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> Hospital in <a href="/wiki/Tampere" title="Tampere">Tampere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> during the 1918 <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Civil_War" title="Finnish Civil War">Finnish Civil War</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Surgery is an invasive technique with the fundamental principle of physical intervention on organs/organ systems/tissues for diagnostic or therapeutic reasons.
</p><p>As a general rule, a procedure is considered surgical when it involves cutting of a person's tissues or closure of a previously sustained wound.  Other procedures that do not necessarily fall under this rubric, such as <a href="/wiki/Angioplasty" title="Angioplasty">angioplasty</a> or <a href="/wiki/Endoscopy" title="Endoscopy">endoscopy</a>, may be considered surgery if they involve "common" surgical procedure or settings, such as use of a sterile environment, <a href="/wiki/Anesthesia" title="Anesthesia">anesthesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antiseptic" title="Antiseptic">antiseptic</a> conditions, typical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surgical_instruments" title="Surgical instruments">surgical instruments</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suturing" title="Suturing">suturing</a> or <a href="/wiki/Surgical_staple" title="Surgical staple">stapling</a>.  All forms of surgery are considered invasive procedures; so-called "noninvasive surgery" usually refers to an excision that does not penetrate the structure being excised (e.g. laser ablation of the cornea) or to a radiosurgical procedure (e.g. irradiation of a tumor).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_surgery">Types of surgery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Surgery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Types of surgery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Surgical procedures are commonly categorized by urgency, type of procedure, body system involved, the degree of invasiveness, and special instrumentation.
</p>
<ul><li>Based on timing: <a href="/wiki/Elective_surgery" title="Elective surgery">Elective surgery</a> is done to correct a non-life-threatening condition, and is carried out at the person's request, subject to the surgeon's and the surgical facility's availability. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-elective_surgery" title="Semi-elective surgery">semi-elective surgery</a> is one that must be done to avoid permanent disability or death, but can be postponed for a short time. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emergency_surgery" title="Emergency surgery">Emergency surgery</a> is surgery which must be done without any delay to prevent death or serious disabilities and/or loss of limbs and functions.</li>
<li>Based on purpose: <a href="/wiki/Exploratory_surgery" title="Exploratory surgery">Exploratory surgery</a> is performed to aid or confirm a diagnosis. Therapeutic surgery treats a previously diagnosed condition. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmetic_surgery#Cosmetic_surgery" title="Cosmetic surgery">Cosmetic surgery</a> is done to subjectively improve the appearance of an otherwise normal structure.</li></ul>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Resection"></span>
</p>
<ul><li>By type of procedure: <a href="/wiki/Amputation" title="Amputation">Amputation</a> involves cutting off a body part, usually a limb or digit; castration is also an example. <b>Resection</b> is the removal of all of an internal organ or body part, or a key part (lung lobe; liver quadrant) of such an organ or body part that has its own name or code designation. A <a href="/wiki/Segmental_resection" title="Segmental resection">segmental resection</a> can be of a smaller region of an organ such as a <a href="/wiki/Lobes_of_liver" title="Lobes of liver">hepatic segment</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Bronchopulmonary_segment" title="Bronchopulmonary segment">bronchopulmonary segment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCI_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCI-3">[2]</a></sup> <b>Excision</b> is the cutting out or removal of only part of an organ, tissue, or other body part from the person. <b>Extirpation</b> is the complete excision or surgical destruction of a body part.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Replantation" title="Replantation">Replantation</a> involves reattaching a severed body part. <a href="/wiki/Reconstructive_surgery" title="Reconstructive surgery">Reconstructive surgery</a> involves reconstruction of an injured, mutilated, or deformed part of the body. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organ_transplant" title="Organ transplant">Transplant</a> surgery is the replacement of an organ or body part by insertion of another from different human (or animal) into the person undergoing surgery. Removing an organ or body part from a live human or animal for use in transplant is also a type of surgery.</li>
<li>By body part: When surgery is performed on one organ system or structure, it may be classed by the organ, organ system or tissue involved. Examples include cardiac surgery (performed on the heart), gastrointestinal surgery (performed within the digestive tract and its accessory organs), and orthopedic surgery (performed on bones or muscles).</li>
<li>By degree of invasiveness of surgical procedures: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minimally-invasive_procedures" title="Minimally-invasive procedures">Minimally-invasive surgery</a> involves smaller outer incisions to insert miniaturized instruments within a body cavity or structure, as in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laparoscopic_surgery" title="Laparoscopic surgery">laparoscopic surgery</a> or <a href="/wiki/Angioplasty" title="Angioplasty">angioplasty</a>. By contrast, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_surgery" title="Open surgery">open surgical procedure</a> such as a <a href="/wiki/Laparotomy" title="Laparotomy">laparotomy</a> requires a large incision to access the area of interest.</li>
<li>By equipment used: <a href="/wiki/Laser_surgery" title="Laser surgery">Laser surgery</a> involves use of a <a href="/wiki/Laser" title="Laser">laser</a> for cutting tissue instead of a <a href="/wiki/Scalpel" title="Scalpel">scalpel</a> or similar surgical instruments. <a href="/wiki/Microsurgery" title="Microsurgery">Microsurgery</a> involves the use of an operating <a href="/wiki/Microscope" title="Microscope">microscope</a> for the surgeon to see small structures. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robotic_surgery" title="Robotic surgery">Robotic surgery</a> makes use of a surgical <a href="/wiki/Robot" title="Robot">robot</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Da_Vinci_Surgical_System" title="Da Vinci Surgical System">Da Vinci</a> or the <a href="/wiki/ZEUS_robotic_surgical_system" title="ZEUS robotic surgical system">ZEUS robotic surgical systems</a>, to control the instrumentation under the direction of the surgeon.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Surgery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_surgical_procedures" title="List of surgical procedures">List of surgical procedures</a></div>
<ul><li>Excision surgery names often start with a name for the organ to be excised (cut out) and end in <b>-ectomy</b>.</li>
<li>Procedures involving cutting into an organ or tissue end in <b>-otomy</b>.  A surgical procedure cutting through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abdominal" title="Abdominal">abdominal</a> wall to gain access to the <a href="/wiki/Abdominal_cavity" title="Abdominal cavity">abdominal cavity</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Laparotomy" title="Laparotomy">laparotomy</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minimally_invasive_surgery#Minimally_invasive_procedure" title="Minimally invasive surgery">Minimally invasive procedures</a>, involving small incisions through which an endoscope is inserted, end in <b>-oscopy</b>.  For example, such surgery in the abdominal cavity is called <a href="/wiki/Laparoscopy" title="Laparoscopy">laparoscopy</a>.</li>
<li>Procedures for formation of a permanent or semi-permanent opening called a <a href="/wiki/Stoma_(medicine)" title="Stoma (medicine)">stoma</a> in the body end in <b>-ostomy</b>.</li>
<li>Reconstruction, plastic or cosmetic surgery of a body part starts with a name for the body part to be reconstructed and ends in <b>-oplasty</b>.  <i>Rhino</i> is used as a prefix for "nose", therefore a <i><a href="/wiki/Rhinoplasty" title="Rhinoplasty">rhinoplasty</a></i> is reconstructive or cosmetic surgery for the nose.</li>
<li>Repair of damaged or congenital abnormal structure ends in <b>-rraphy</b>.</li>
<li>Reoperation (return to the operating room) refers to a return to the operating theater after an initial surgery is performed to re-address an aspect of patient care best treated surgically. Reasons for reoperation include persistent bleeding after surgery, development of or persistence of infection.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Description_of_surgical_procedure">Description of surgical procedure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Surgery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Description of surgical procedure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Surgery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inpatient" title="Inpatient">Inpatient</a> surgery is performed in a hospital, and the person undergoing surgery stays at least one night in the hospital after the surgery. <a href="/wiki/Outpatient_surgery" title="Outpatient surgery">Outpatient surgery</a> occurs in a hospital outpatient department or freestanding ambulatory surgery center, and the person who had surgery is discharged the same working day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LemosIAAS2006_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-LemosIAAS2006-5">[4]</a></sup> Office surgery occurs in a physician's office, and the person is discharged the same working day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Twersky2008_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Twersky2008-6">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>At a <a href="/wiki/Hospital" title="Hospital">hospital</a>, modern surgery is often performed in an <a href="/wiki/Operating_theater" title="Operating theater">operating theater</a> using <a href="/wiki/Surgical_instrument" title="Surgical instrument">surgical instruments</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Operating_table" title="Operating table">operating table</a>, and other equipment. Among United States hospitalizations for non-maternal and non-neonatal conditions in 2012, more than one-fourth of stays and half of hospital costs involved stays that included operating room (OR) procedures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> The environment and procedures used in surgery are governed by the principles of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aseptic_technique" title="Aseptic technique">aseptic technique</a>: the strict separation of "sterile" (free of microorganisms) things from "unsterile" or "contaminated" things.  All surgical instruments must be <a href="/wiki/Sterilization_(microbiology)" title="Sterilization (microbiology)">sterilized</a>, and an instrument must be replaced or re-sterilized if it becomes contaminated (i.e. handled in an unsterile manner, or allowed to touch an unsterile surface). Operating room staff must wear sterile attire (<a href="/wiki/Scrubs_(clothing)" title="Scrubs (clothing)">scrubs</a>, a scrub cap, a sterile surgical gown, sterile latex or non-latex polymer gloves and a surgical mask), and they must scrub hands and arms with an approved disinfectant agent before each procedure.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Preoperative_care">Preoperative care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Surgery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Preoperative care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Preoperative_care" title="Preoperative care">Preoperative care</a></div>
<p>Prior to surgery, the person is given a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_examination" title="Medical examination">medical examination</a>, receives certain pre-operative tests, and their <a href="/wiki/Physical_fitness" title="Physical fitness">physical status</a> is rated according to the <a href="/wiki/ASA_physical_status_classification_system" title="ASA physical status classification system">ASA physical status classification system</a>. If these results are satisfactory, the person requiring surgery signs a consent form and is given a surgical clearance. If the procedure is expected to result in significant blood loss, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autologous" title="Autologous">autologous</a> <a href="/wiki/Blood_donation" title="Blood donation">blood donation</a> may be made some weeks prior to surgery. If the surgery involves the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digestive_system" title="Digestive system">digestive system</a>, the person requiring surgery may be instructed to perform a <a href="/wiki/Whole_bowel_irrigation" title="Whole bowel irrigation">bowel prep</a> by drinking a solution of <a href="/wiki/Polyethylene_glycol" title="Polyethylene glycol">polyethylene glycol</a> the night before the procedure. People preparing for surgery are also instructed to abstain from food or drink (an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nil_per_os" title="Nil per os">NPO order</a> after midnight on the night before the procedure), to minimize the effect of stomach contents on pre-operative medications and reduce the risk of aspiration if the person vomits during or after the procedure.
</p><p>Some medical systems have a practice of routinely performing chest x-rays before surgery. The premise behind this practice is that the physician might discover some unknown medical condition which would complicate the surgery, and that upon discovering this with the chest x-ray, the physician would adapt the surgery practice accordingly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACRfive_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACRfive-8">[7]</a></sup> However, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specialty_(medicine)" title="Specialty (medicine)">medical specialty</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Professional_organizations" title="Professional organizations">professional organizations</a> recommend against routine pre-operative <a href="/wiki/Chest_radiograph" title="Chest radiograph">chest x-rays</a> for people who have an unremarkable medical history and presented with a physical exam which did not indicate a chest x-ray.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACRfive_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-ACRfive-8">[7]</a></sup> Routine x-ray examination is more likely to result in problems like misdiagnosis, overtreatment, or other negative outcomes than it is to result in a benefit to the person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACRfive_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-ACRfive-8">[7]</a></sup> Likewise, other tests including <a href="/wiki/Complete_blood_count" title="Complete blood count">complete blood count</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prothrombin_time" title="Prothrombin time">prothrombin time</a>, <a href="/wiki/Partial_thromboplastin_time" title="Partial thromboplastin time">partial thromboplastin time</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basic_metabolic_panel" title="Basic metabolic panel">basic metabolic panel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Urinalysis" title="Urinalysis">urinalysis</a> should not be done unless the results of these tests can help evaluate surgical risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ASCPfive_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-ASCPfive-9">[8]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Staging_for_surgery">Staging for surgery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Surgery&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Staging for surgery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox
